## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / mathematical biology (population dynamics)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an instantaneous population growth rate driven by current population size P and possibly time t, which is the standard setup for single-species population-dynamics ODE models with density dependence, harvesting, and environmental forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (constant per-capita growth rate in unlimited environment)
- Linear immigration/emigration: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (intrinsic growth plus constant net inflow/outflow)
- Density-dependent (Verhulst) growth-rate form: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (self-limitation via carrying capacity ~ 1/c1)
- Gompertz growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (per-capita growth declines logarithmically with size)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P) ** c2) (flexible density dependence; c2 shapes curvature near carrying capacity)
- Power-law birth–death balance: dP_dt = c0 * P ** c1 - c2 * P ** c3 (separate scaling of recruitment and losses with population size)
- Exponential crowding (Ricker-continuous analogue): dP_dt = c0 * P * (exp(c1 - c2 * P) - 1) (rapid decline in per-capita growth with crowding)
- Allee effect with carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (low-density suppression plus high-density limitation)
- Proportional harvesting (effort proportional to P): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (harvest mortality proportional to population)
- Constant-yield harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (fixed offtake independent of population size)
- Seasonal intrinsic growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (environmental forcing modulates per-capita growth over time)
- Seasonal carrying capacity / competition strength: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4)) * P) (time-varying density dependence)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If (dP_dt / P) is approximately constant across P, favor dP_dt ≈ c * P (density-independent growth).
- If dP_dt increases with P at low P but crosses zero near a finite P, favor factors like (1 - c * P) indicating a carrying capacity.
- If (dP_dt / P) decreases roughly linearly with P, prefer logistic-rate structure P * (1 - c * P); if it decreases like log(P), prefer Gompertz P * log(c / P).
- If growth is negative at very low P but positive at intermediate P, include an Allee factor like (c * P - 1) multiplying the growth term.
- A persistent negative offset in dP_dt at large P suggests constant-yield harvesting (subtract c), while losses proportional to P suggest subtracting c * P.
- Non-integer powers in P (e.g., P**c) indicate allometric or aggregation effects (recruitment/mortality scaling nonlinearly with population).
- An exponential-in-P suppression term (e.g., exp(-c * P)) suggests very strong crowding or resource limitation that steepens with density.
- If residuals vs t show periodicity, include sinusoidal forcing in coefficients (e.g., c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) on either P or P*(1-cP) terms.

### 0) What the GT depends on

\[
0.8450821(-1+P/5.115386)(1-P/34.438862)P \;+\; 0.8450821(1-e^{-0.09687266P})P
\]
Key properties:

- **No \(t\) dependence at all**.
- It is a function of \(P\) only, of the form
  \[
  F(P)= A\cdot P\cdot(\text{quadratic in }P)\;+\;A\cdot P\;-\;A\cdot P e^{-kP}
  \]
  i.e. it contains an explicit **\(P e^{-kP}\)** term with \(k=0.09687266\neq 0\).
- Therefore any matching candidate must be able (after parameter choices) to produce **exactly** a term proportional to \(P e^{-kP}\) (with negative sign), plus polynomial-in-\(P\) terms, and must eliminate any \(t\)-dependence.

---

## 1) Candidates that include \(t\)
Any candidate with unavoidable \(t\)-dependence cannot match, unless its \(t\)-dependent part can be made identically zero by setting a coefficient to 0.

- **1** has \(c6*exp(P*c7)*sin(c8*t+c9)\). Can set \(c6=0\) to remove \(t\). Remaining terms are polynomial + \(\sin(\log(\cdot))\), no \(P e^{-kP}\). **No**.
- **2** has \(c2\sin(c3 t+c4)\). Set \(c2=0\). Remaining polynomial + \(\sin(\log(\cdot))\), no \(P e^{-kP}\). **No**.
- **3** has \(P^{c2}c3 e^{c4 t}\). Set \(c3=0\) to remove. Still no \(P e^{-kP}\). **No**.
- **4** has \(c5 e^{Pc6}\cos(c7 t+c8)\). Set \(c5=0\). Left with polynomial + \(P e^{P c4}\) (positive exponent form), cannot make \(e^{-kP}\) appear because exponent is \(+Pc4\) but could set \(c4=-k\) giving \(P e^{-kP}\); however the term is \(P*c3*exp(P*c4)\) which could match the exponential part, but GT also has a *cubic polynomial* part \(P\cdot(\text{quadratic})\) = up to \(P^3\). Candidate 4 has only \(P^2 c0 + P c1 + P c2\) plus the exponential term: **no \(P^3\)** possible. **No**.
- **5** similarly: can kill \(\sin\) by \(c5=0\), but still lacks \(P^3\). **No**.
- **6** has \(\log(c7\exp(Pc8+c9 t)+1)\). To remove \(t\), need \(c6=0\) or \(c9=0\). If \(c6=0\), no exponential term. If \(c9=0\), still \(\log(c7 e^{Pc8}+1)=\log(c7)+Pc8\) only if the “+1” weren’t there; with +1 it’s not linear. In any case cannot produce \(P e^{-kP}\). **No**.
- **7** has \(c6 e^{c7 t}\). Set \(c6=0\). No \(P e^{-kP}\). **No**.
- **8–10,12–15,17–19,21,27–30,34–37,39–40,49–50,72,84–86,88–89,92–94,97,99,101–102,106,114–116,118–125,126,128–132** all contain \(t\) in various ways. In every case you can potentially zero out the \(t\)-dependent term by setting its coefficient to 0, but then what remains is built from polynomials, logs, sines, rationals, or \(P e^{+aP}\) terms. None of these families can exactly reproduce the GT’s combination of a **cubic polynomial in \(P\)** plus a **\(-\text{const}\cdot P e^{-kP}\)** term, unless the candidate explicitly contains both a \(P^3\) capability and a \(P e^{-kP}\) capability. The only candidates that even have \(P e^{(\cdot)P}\) are those with \(P*c3*exp(P*c4)\) or \(c2*exp(P*c3)\) etc; among those, none also allow an independent \(P^3\) term (they top out at \(P^2\) unless they have \(P^3\) explicitly). So all these are **No**.

(We’ll be more explicit about the “best-looking” exponential forms below.)

## 2) Candidates without \(t\) (or with removable \(t\)) but needing GT’s structure

### 2.1 Need a \(P^3\) term
GT’s first part expands to a cubic polynomial in \(P\) (because \(P\cdot(-1+P/a)\cdot(1-P/b)\) is \(P\) times a quadratic). So any match must be able to generate a \(P^3\) term.

Scan candidates: almost all start with \(P^2*c0 + P*c1 + \dots\). That means **maximum polynomial degree 2** unless there is an explicit \(P^3\) or a product that yields \(P^3\). The only explicit \(P^3\) candidates are **49,52,75,100,107,120,122,127,130,132** (and a few with \(P^3\) in rational form).

But GT has **no \(t\)** and also has **\(-P e^{-kP}\)**. Let’s check these \(P^3\) candidates:

- **49**: \(P^3 c0 e^{c1 t} + P^2 c2 + Pc3 + c4\). Remove \(t\) by \(c1=0\) gives \(P^3 c0 + P^2 c2 + Pc3 + c4\): purely polynomial, **no \(P e^{-kP}\)**. **No**.
- **52**: polynomial + \( \sin(\log(\cdot))\). No exponential decay term. **No**.
- **75**: rational with denominator \(P c1 + c2\). Cannot equal a polynomial-plus-\(P e^{-kP}\) for all \(P\). **No**.
- **100**: polynomial + \(P c7 e^{P c8}\) (positive/negative exponent possible). Has \(P^3\) and \(P e^{Pc8}\), good. But it lacks a **\(P^2\)** coefficient flexibility? It has multiple \(P^2\) terms yes. However GT also has a **plain \(+A P\)** term and a **cubic polynomial with specific coefficients**; those could be matched by choosing polynomial coefficients. The problem: GT’s exponential term is \(-A P e^{-kP}\) and there is **no constant term** in GT. Candidate 100 has no constant term, good. So could we set \(c8=-k\) and \(c7=-A\) to match the exponential part, and tune polynomial coefficients to match the cubic polynomial part? Candidate 100 polynomial part is:
  \[
  P^3 c0 + P^2(c1+c2+c3) + P(c4+c5+c6)
  \]
  That can match any cubic polynomial with no constant term (3 degrees of freedom). GT’s polynomial part indeed is some cubic with no constant term. So **candidate 100 actually can match** the full GT if we can match the polynomial coefficients exactly and set the exponential term correctly.
  
  Wait: GT polynomial part is not arbitrary; it is:
  \[
  A\cdot P(-1+P/a)(1-P/b) + A\cdot P
  \]
  which simplifies to a cubic with no constant term. Candidate 100 can represent any such cubic (choose \(c0\) for \(P^3\), choose \(c1+c2+c3\) for \(P^2\), choose \(c4+c5+c6\) for \(P\)). Exponential term \(P c7 e^{P c8}\) can match \(-A P e^{-kP}\) by \(c7=-A\), \(c8=-k\). This seems feasible.

So candidate **100** is a strong match.

Let’s ensure no hidden mismatch: GT has exactly one exponential term \(-A P e^{-kP}\) and candidate 100 has exactly one exponential term \(+P c7 e^{P c8}\). Good. GT has no extra nonlinearities. Candidate 100 has none besides that. So candidate 100 **can be made identical**.

Therefore we already have a match; still, quickly check other \(P^3\) candidates:

- **107**: rational \(\frac{P^3 c0 + P^2(\cdots)+P(\cdots)}{P c1+1}\) not equal to polynomial+exponential. **No**.
- **120** includes \(t\) and log term; cannot reduce to GT without killing essential parts; also wrong functional form. **No**.
- **122** includes \(e^{c1 t}\); setting \(c1=0\) gives polynomial only. **No**.
- **127** rational. **No**.
- **130** polynomial + \(P\log(\cdot)\). **No**.
- **132** polynomial + \(P\log(\cdot)\). **No**.

Thus the only viable is **100**.

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG3)
============================================================
GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*(c6 - exp(-c7*P))*P
Candidates evaluated: 132
Matched candidate IDs: [100]
Matched candidates: ["P**3*c0 + P**2*c1 + P**2*c2 + P**2*c3 + P*c4 + P*c5 + P*c6 + P*c7*exp(P*c8)"]

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare it with each candidate.

**GT expression:**
```
0.845*(P/5.115 - 1)*(1 - P/34.44)*P + 0.845*(1 - exp(-0.0969*P))*P
```

Let me expand this:
- First term: `0.845*(P/5.115 - 1)*(1 - P/34.44)*P`
  - `= 0.845*P*(P/5.115 - 1)*(1 - P/34.44)`
  - `= 0.845*P*[P/5.115 - P²/(5.115*34.44) - 1 + P/34.44]`
  - `= 0.845*P*[-P²/176.14 + P(1/5.115 + 1/34.44) - 1]`
  - `= 0.845*[-P³/176.14 + P²(0.1955 + 0.02904) - P]`
  - `= 0.845*[-P³/176.14 + 0.2245*P² - P]`
  - `= -0.004797*P³ + 0.1897*P² - 0.845*P`

- Second term: `0.845*(1 - exp(-0.0969*P))*P`
  - `= 0.845*P - 0.845*P*exp(-0.0969*P)`

**Combined GT:**
```
-0.004797*P³ + 0.1897*P² - 0.845*P + 0.845*P - 0.845*P*exp(-0.0969*P)
= -0.004797*P³ + 0.1897*P² - 0.845*P*exp(-0.0969*P)
```

So GT = `a*P³ + b*P² + c*P*exp(d*P)` where a < 0, b > 0, c < 0, d < 0.

Key observations:
- GT has **no dependence on t** (time-independent)
- GT consists of: P³ term, P² term, and P*exp(negative*P) term
- No sin, cos, log terms

Now let me check candidates that are time-independent and have the right basis functions.

**Candidates with P³, P², P*exp(P) structure (no t dependence):**

The form `P²*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2 + P*c3*exp(P*c4)` simplifies to `P²*c0 + P*(c1+c2) + P*c3*exp(P*c4)`. This is missing P³.

But `P²*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*exp(P*c3)` = `P²*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*exp(P*c3)` — also missing P³.

Wait, let me reconsider. The GT is `a*P³ + b*P² + c*P*exp(d*P)`. I need candidates that can produce a P³ term.

**Candidate 112:** `P²*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*exp(P*c3)` — Missing P³. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 100:** `P³*c0 + P²*(c1+c2+c3) + P*(c4+c5+c6) + P*c7*exp(P*c8)` — This has P³, P², P, and P*exp(P). GT has no standalone P term (the linear terms cancelled). But we can set the P coefficient to 0. So this matches the structure: `a*P³ + b*P² + c*P*exp(d*P)`. ✓

Let me verify: set c4+c5+c6 = 0, and we get `P³*c0 + P²*(c1+c2+c3) + P*c7*exp(P*c8)`. This matches GT form!

**Candidate 100 verdict: [MATCH]**

Let me check other P³ candidates similarly:

**Candidate 109:** `P²*(c0+c1) + P*(c2+c3+c6) + P*c4*exp(P*c5)` — No P³. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 110, 113, 60, 63:** All lack P³. [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 107:** `[P³*c0 + P²*(c2+c3+c4) + P*c5]/(P*c1+1)` — rational function, not polynomial+exp. [NO MATCH]

Let me systematically go through all candidates checking for: (1) no t dependence possible, (2) P³ + P² + P*exp(P) structure.

After careful analysis, only **Candidate 100** has the correct basis functions {P³, P², P, P*exp(P)} where the P term can be zeroed.
